  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bffa9944-d6ea-4d0a-8a59-9e02e48f30b5'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

The victims were biologists at Plum Island, a research site rumored to be an incubator for germ warfare.Suddenly, a local double murder takes on shattering global implications -- and thrusts Corey and two extraordinary women into a dangerous search for the secret of PLUM ISLAND....</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">What's going on with DeMille? HIs recent book was a rewrite of an earlier book and was really abysmal. HIs recent book was a rewrite of an earlier book and was really abysmal. Now this one being marketed as if it were new? Both DeMille and his publisher need to rethink their strategy. And maybe DeMille should have had a better financial advisor- he used to be a good writer.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1766428149?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bibi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bibi" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi">Bibi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/50077308-plum-island">review of another edition</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33411728-bibi?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1766428149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2920453719881672404"><blockquote><b>Keep in mind that I read this book a little over a decade and a half ago, yet the story is as vivid today as it was then. Damn. That is the genius that is Nelson Demille.</b><br/><br/>The book starts with a convalescing John Corey, formerly of the NYPD, who wants nothing more than to drink beer while relaxing at his Uncle's Long Island beach house. When two prominent scientists (who worked at a secret research facility on Plum Island) are murdered, John is drafted to investigate the deaths. With acerbic wit a</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2920453719881672404" style="display:none"><blockquote><b>Keep in mind that I read this book a little over a decade and a half ago, yet the story is as vivid today as it was then. Damn. That is the genius that is Nelson Demille.</b><br /><br />The book starts with a convalescing John Corey, formerly of the NYPD, who wants nothing more than to drink beer while relaxing at his Uncle's Long Island beach house. When two prominent scientists (who worked at a secret research facility on Plum Island) are murdered, John is drafted to investigate the deaths. With acerbic wit and deliberate misdirection, he goes on to solve the case.<br /><br /><b>The humor in this book was unexpected yet it was exactly what was required in order to elevate the story beyond the mundane.</b><br /><br />Be sure to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33825.The_Lion_s_Game__John_Corey___2_" title="The Lion's Game (John Corey, #2) by Nelson DeMille" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lion's Game</a> as well, which is a book that, although published in 2000, portends the 9/11 tragedy with uncanny accuracy.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="2920453719881672404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1412180712" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1412180712" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1412180712?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">swinging dicks </span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1412180712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1293718467332369153">With any review I do, I ask myself a single question: "How much do you care whether or not people read this book." This time, the answer is not so simple. I honestly have no idea whether or not people are interested in Nelson DeMille. Dude has a following. He doesn't need my help. Also, he's not terrible, so I don't feel the need to be satirical with my review. He's somewhere between Greg Iles and Howard Stern. Basically, this guy writes really verbose books for middle-aged men. There's some men</span>
  <span id="freeText1293718467332369153" style="display:none">With any review I do, I ask myself a single question: "How much do you care whether or not people read this book." This time, the answer is not so simple. I honestly have no idea whether or not people are interested in Nelson DeMille. Dude has a following. He doesn't need my help. Also, he's not terrible, so I don't feel the need to be satirical with my review. He's somewhere between Greg Iles and Howard Stern. Basically, this guy writes really verbose books for middle-aged men. There's some mention of sex or tits or ass on every page. Much beer is swilled. Everyone cracks wise. If you like that kind of thing, you should enjoy yourself. If not, you'll likely hate it. <br /><br />I <i>should have</i> hated this book. It was predictable, the comedy wasn't always funny, and the writing was basic and repetitive. The main character is a womanizer who sees every woman he comes across as an object to be filled, and the women he meets along the way actually like that about him. There's one point where a woman says, (I'm paraphrasing) "You're not like most men, John. Most men want to know more about me. You just want to have sex. I like that about you." I had to laugh. I know some of you ladies like a stiff dick just as much as we like a place to put it, but this came off as silly in places. None of the women in this book could be confused with strong, independent females. One lady who's a homicide detective allows the MC to leave her behind because she might get her fragile little self hurt. Oh fuck off. <br /><br />The odd part is, I never wanted to stop reading, and the best excuse I have for that is this analogy. <br /><br />You know that one stupid-as-fuck friend we all have? Well, if you don't, you're probably that friend. Just saying. Anyballs, so we all have that one friend who's dumber than a load of bricks dropped on a horny ostrich, but they are fun to be around. If you need a math problem done, you're not going to call Nelson. But if you're in a mood to drink thirty beers and burn some shit, Nelson's definitely your go to guy. You don't invite him around your girlfriend because he's rude and disgusting. But if you're ever expecting a tussle with a buncha inebriated rednecks, Nelson's gonna fuck 'em up for you. Yeah, that's this book. <br /><br />And yes. To address the 800-pound swinging dick in the room, yes, this book is overlong. No book of this kind should be almost 600 pages. But, once again, I never once wanted to stop reading. Take that for what it's worth.<br /><br />In summation: If Columbo took all season to solve a case instead of a single episode, and then, while he was attempting to solve the crime, he catcalled every passing female and fucked the ones who didn't run away, this book would be the result. You're either going to love it or hate it. Me? I'm in the middle. I'd read more about this character, but I'd have to be in the right mood for him. You ladies have your Mommy Porn and such. Guys have Nelson DeMille. As far as I see it, we're even. <br /><br /><b>Final Judgment: The most sexist thing you're likely to enjoy.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1293718467332369153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167609194?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/5411976-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167609194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16608542840426745837">I will forever remember this book as the one I painstakingly read in tiny font, all 574 pages of it, and found that it could have been shortened to less than half of the pages without reducing any substance or plot whatsoever. What a waste of time.<br/>I was expecting some big story or conspiracy to unfold, as that's what I was lead to believe by reading the back cover. Dead scientists who used to work in an animal research facility, dealing with viruses and bacteria--sounds promising isn't it? Too b</span>
  <span id="freeText16608542840426745837" style="display:none">I will forever remember this book as the one I painstakingly read in tiny font, all 574 pages of it, and found that it could have been shortened to less than half of the pages without reducing any substance or plot whatsoever. What a waste of time.<br />I was expecting some big story or conspiracy to unfold, as that's what I was lead to believe by reading the back cover. Dead scientists who used to work in an animal research facility, dealing with viruses and bacteria--sounds promising isn't it? Too bad, the problem and investigation part of the story filled probably only half of the book. The rest? An overly-deep exploration into the main character's thinking. No kidding. If you want to read this book, expect to read the main character's dialectical dialogue with himself throughout most of the book. Though thankfully this main character's pretty funny, so I did find myself still being entertained at times. <br />However, back to my expectation about how the story's going to unfold, I got disappointed again. I was expecting something big in the plot, maybe a twist, maybe something that involves risk to the bigger community, maybe some more action, maybe some secret--but the answer to the mystery was just personal, relating to the victims themselves. <br />The way the story unfolds is slow; and there's lots of "spaces" in the story that are filled with the main character's conversation with himself. I couldn't believe I was already past halfway and the story told very little about the mystery itself. At that point though, I felt that I knew the main character so well I could predict what he's going to do next.<br />All in all, don't expect this to be a fast-paced thriller/mystery but expect this to be a light read about your usual murder investigation with a somewhat-funny main character that you'll know better than your mum by the end of this book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16608542840426745837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_96778550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96778550" />
    <a title="Jess" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/901103-jess"><img alt="Jess" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514746183p2/901103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96778550?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess" href="/user/show/901103-jess">Jess</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/901103-jess?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/901103-jess?shelf=nl-5-challenge">nl-5-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/901103-jess?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96778550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17349622506210951588">I probably wouldn't have picked up this book if it weren't for a group I was in suggesting it. I have never read anything by this author, and to be honest I never really heard of him before this.<br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book. It started off a little slowly, and the main character John Corey was such a sarcastic SOB that he was great! I liked his style and his humor... although I'm not sure I was really supposed to like him. John is a homicide detective with the NYPD and is currently recuperating in</span>
  <span id="freeText17349622506210951588" style="display:none">I probably wouldn't have picked up this book if it weren't for a group I was in suggesting it. I have never read anything by this author, and to be honest I never really heard of him before this.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. It started off a little slowly, and the main character John Corey was such a sarcastic SOB that he was great! I liked his style and his humor... although I'm not sure I was really supposed to like him. John is a homicide detective with the NYPD and is currently recuperating in the North Fork of Long Island from being shot three times. He is approached by the local sheriff Max to help with a double murder. John is reluctant to help, and the only reason he does help is because he knows the victims.<br /><br />The case itself, a wife and husband are found outside their home dead. The next door neighbor insists that they came home late on their boat, but never heard the gun going off. The problem that makes this case so dangerous, the couple worked on Plum Island which contains a virus and bacteria research facility. Of course they only look at diseases that affect animals, because the US government has signed a policy stating they do not do germ warfare research. Yeah. Okay. So the feds, the CIA, the local police and whoever else has a badge, is searching to see if the couple was killed because of their job on the island. Did they steal a deadly virus that can wipe out the world, did they steal a vaccine so they could make themselves billions of dollars or is this just a case of a home burglary gone wrong. John Corey thinks he knows, and he thinks that he is the only one who can solve this case.<br /><br />After the beginning, maybe about 20-30 pages, the book really picked up the pace and John made the book interesting. His theories were intriguing, and his humor and sarcasm kept me in touch with his character. I liked that I wasn't able to guess what was really going on, and that there were a few surprises along the way. I also liked the setting of the book and that it's in close proximity to where I live, and I have actually been to some of the places mentioned. <br /><br />I just found out that this is the first in a series, so I'm going to look into the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17349622506210951588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_42775353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42775353" />
    <a title="Leah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/756706-leah"><img alt="Leah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257351490p2/756706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42775353?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/756706-leah">Leah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/756706-leah?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42775353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4135014206757788866">My dad works on Plum Island...the real one. I was dying to read this book because it's about my home on Long Island and because I know quite a bit about PLum Island, so I wanted to see what Demille would do with the story. Indulge my rant, if you will...<br/><br/>Plum Island is a biosafety level 3 lab off the coast of the north fork of LI that studies animal deseases like Foot & Mouth, Mad Cow, etc., and does everything they can to keep these diseases out of the US and protect the livestock in our country</span>
  <span id="freeText4135014206757788866" style="display:none">My dad works on Plum Island...the real one. I was dying to read this book because it's about my home on Long Island and because I know quite a bit about PLum Island, so I wanted to see what Demille would do with the story. Indulge my rant, if you will...<br /><br />Plum Island is a biosafety level 3 lab off the coast of the north fork of LI that studies animal deseases like Foot &amp; Mouth, Mad Cow, etc., and does everything they can to keep these diseases out of the US and protect the livestock in our country. The island is shrouded in mystery because the public is not allowed there and much of what they work on is only know in the world of science. People in the local community are often skeptical of the work they do, creating such lovely rumors of animal abuse and biological warfare studies. <br /><br />DeMille takes hysteria to new levels and heights of impossibility by fabricating a story that is not only dull at times, but completely UNbeleivable at others. In the story, the lab is classified as a Zone 5 (which doesn't exist in the real world), and contains such lovely biohazards as ebola, anthrax, and every other weapon known to science that can wipe out entire populations with a sneeze. The scientists on the island are also allowed to bring their own boats to work, and people from the local historical society have been conducting archaeological digs around the island. Ridiculous.<br /><br />The main character of the book is trying to solve a murder, but don't bother reading the story if you don't like chauvinistic males who characterize themselves as close-minded pricks who only want a good lay. I was annoyed through most of the book simply because of the main character's inner dialogue. Not to mention the fact that he is a cop who sleeps with witnesses, and nearly murders the main suspect. REALLY?! Is this a joke? <br /><br />Anyway, if you're from the North Fork, this book will annoy you. If you're from anywhere else and you're a woman, this book will annoy you. If you're a dude who sleeps around, and lives by the mantra "ignorance is bliss" this book is for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4135014206757788866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_513844047" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/513844047" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513844047?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513844047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15465207558508396433">I sat here for a good while considering what to rate this book. I came very close to giving it 5 stars and am still thinking it over (I reserve the right to come back and up the rating if I decide to, LOL).<br/><br/>This is an excellent book in a genre that I don't usually find my favorite. It's well written with a likeable yet infuriating protagonist. (Not too unlike Harry Dresden if that's a reference you're familiar with.) He does hit one of my annoyance buttons which I'll mention later under a spoiler</span>
  <span id="freeText15465207558508396433" style="display:none">I sat here for a good while considering what to rate this book. I came very close to giving it 5 stars and am still thinking it over (I reserve the right to come back and up the rating if I decide to, LOL).<br /><br />This is an excellent book in a genre that I don't usually find my favorite. It's well written with a likeable yet infuriating protagonist. (Not too unlike Harry Dresden if that's a reference you're familiar with.) He does hit one of my annoyance buttons which I'll mention later under a spoiler warning. <br /><br />What else, well the plot is a good one with hook that while not new can be tricky to use well <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I mean pirate treasure can get hokey fast <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The characters while not exactly jumping off the page are painted in true and at times even vibrant colors and remain true to "themselves" throughout the book. You don't get deus ex machina kinds of "getting out of a corner" writing and the clues lead to an answer that works. In other words you don't put everything together and come to a conclusion only to find that there's some vital clue you never got and the culprit turns out to be the old gardener who you met and saw for 5 lines in the second chapter. <br /><br />While not an action book this is an intense book and will I think hold your interest. The protagonist is snarky, sarcastic, and a general <s>smart ass</s> errr smart aleck...wise guy who can't tell the right time to just keep his mouth shut...a man after my own heart in other words, though even I rolled my eyes a few times. I mean why borrow trouble? And believe me, John does.<br /><br />This is my introduction to DeMille's work which I've somehow missed up till now. I don't think it will be my last (baring unexpected demise or something). So well written, nice mystery/thriller with a satisfying hook and plot, I can recommend this one wholeheartedly. <br /><br /><br />***Major Spoiler Below****<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Those of you who know me know I'm not a romance fan and an all consuming romance will ruin a book for me in a heartbeat. I hate wading through a primarily romantic yarn to get to a plot buried in the love story up to it's proverbial nose. Here we get a romance and I give the author props. I not only let my guard down but "he got me". My initial distrust of the "love interest" (thinking she might be in on the "plot") gave way finally to a okay I like her and I hope she isn't one of the "bad guys" and then after I got sort of involved...he killed her. I was I admit surprised, and not completely positively. I had come to care about the character and the protagonist. DeMille did a good job and as unpleasant as it is to lose a character you like It shows I got involved in the book.<br /><br />Doesn't happen to me often in this context. This book is well written. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_281835167" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/281835167" />
    <a title="LeAnne: GeezerMom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7862560-leanne-geezermom"><img alt="LeAnne: GeezerMom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514579326p2/7862560.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/281835167?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LeAnne: GeezerMom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LeAnne: GeezerMom" href="/user/show/7862560-leanne-geezermom">LeAnne: GeezerMom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7862560-leanne-geezermom?shelf=favorite-fluff">favorite-fluff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer281835167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7596493202385933376">One of my favorite all-time thrillers, this is a fantastic beach book with intrigue, smart-alec humor, biological warfare concerns, and even a touch of love. As a fan of everything Nelson Demille had written to that point, I read Plum Island in 1997, the very month it was published and chomped it down.<br/><br/>Since then, Demille has lately resurrected the main character John Corey another five times as the star of other thrillers, and you may have bumped into him. But this baby remains my fave.<br/><br/>John is a</span>
  <span id="freeText7596493202385933376" style="display:none">One of my favorite all-time thrillers, this is a fantastic beach book with intrigue, smart-alec humor, biological warfare concerns, and even a touch of love. As a fan of everything Nelson Demille had written to that point, I read Plum Island in 1997, the very month it was published and chomped it down.<br /><br />Since then, Demille has lately resurrected the main character John Corey another five times as the star of other thrillers, and you may have bumped into him. But this baby remains my fave.<br /><br />John is a NY detective who was shot in the line of duty and is on temporary disability leave. His uncle has a house out on Long Island where Corey has visited over the years, and he spends his convalescence sipping some self-medication on the back porch and gawping at boaters who pass by. He's bored but healing up.<br /><br />John gets pulled from this quiet by the local constable who asks him to consult on the double-murder of a couple he's familiar with, seemingly a house robbery gone wrong. Except, of course, the constable knows zippo about murder.<br /><br />Because the husband and wife both work at Plum Island (former site for biological warfare research), the feds slip into the investigation under the auspices of the Department of Agriculture. A female homicide detective from an adjoining county enters the picture, and between the now-four investigators, all sorts of fire hydrants get peed on with most of the men jockeying for control.<br /><br />What is so interesting about the story is the aspect of the bio-warfare lab - everybody has heard of Lyme Disease, right? Well, the town of Lyme, Connecticut is directly across the sound from Plum Island, and deer - carrying ticks they picked up from the experimental cattle yards on the island - are excellent swimmers. Was Lyme disease created by the USA as a weapon back in the 50s or something? Was anthrax being weaponized here? Dunno! Also, have you seen the movie Silence of the Lambs? The island that Clarice promises that Hannibal can visit is this one... he even comments on it in the movie.<br /><br />At any rate, the intrigue is fun, and the smart-ass-cop-humor is macho and very snarky. Mark this as the very first (and last) time I ever heard a guy refer to his, um, tight pants as a "meat puppet." So yes, if you're a lady or gentleman who might be offended by foul language, sexual activity, touches of vulgarity, and violence - you might skip this.<br /><br />For the rest of you sinners looking for solid entertainment, please introduce yourself to writer <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille" title="Nelson DeMille" rel="nofollow noopener">Nelson DeMille</a>. Maybe take an antibiotic first. 5 stars, favorite-fluff shelf.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7596493202385933376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3439923493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3439923493" />
    <a title="Karl Jorgenson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12413321-karl-jorgenson"><img alt="Karl Jorgenson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584120483p2/12413321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3439923493?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karl Jorgenson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karl Jorgenson" href="/user/show/12413321-karl-jorgenson">Karl Jorgenson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3439923493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15076805673182389737">The opening of the Corey series. DeMille weaves a complicated, but credible plot. Two scientists working at a bio-hazard, isolated government lab are murdered. Could it be terrorism? Theft of horrible pathogens?<br/>An excerpt, relevant to today's pandemic:<br/><br/> 'The last big deadly human influenza epidemic in the world was in 1918. There were about twenty million dead worldwide, including five hundred thousand in the U.S. Based on our present population, U.S. dead would be one and a half million. And the</span>
  <span id="freeText15076805673182389737" style="display:none">The opening of the Corey series. DeMille weaves a complicated, but credible plot. Two scientists working at a bio-hazard, isolated government lab are murdered. Could it be terrorism? Theft of horrible pathogens?<br />An excerpt, relevant to today's pandemic:<br /><br /> 'The last big deadly human influenza epidemic in the world was in 1918. There were about twenty million dead worldwide, including five hundred thousand in the U.S. Based on our present population, U.S. dead would be one and a half million. And the 1918 virus wasn't particularly virulent, and of course travel was much slower and less frequent. Today, the highways and skyways can spread infectious virus around the world in days.'<br /><br />Corey is the ultimate rude, snarky, intolerant New Yorker. He bashes his way through the investigation, abusing everyone in his path, but finding the secrets behind the murders.<br />DeMille does a wonderful job of revealing the layer of the plot and supplies heart-pounding action and a string of surprises in the last chapters.<br />In later books, Corey is married to his bright and long-suffering wife, Kate. He hasn't met her yet in this book, but Corey partners with Beth, a local detective, who is in every meaningful way a clone of Kate. Well, an author can come up with only so many truly distinct personalities. Scott Turow excepted. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15076805673182389737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17799262?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gina" href="/user/show/985335-gina">Gina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780446605403" href="/book/show/685453.Plum_Island">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17799262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10609822702821186564">First book in the series, and I really liked it!<br/><br/>When I found out that DeMille wrote The General's Daughter, I did a little more research on his 'John Corey' series. It seems that he hadn't wanted to write a series, but there were too many of his readers who wanted another John Corey book. He'd been afraid of his female readers; what they'd think of John as a character. He's cocky, tactless, crude, and a real ass, but I adored him. I loved how his mind worked, how he processed what he saw, what h</span>
  <span id="freeText10609822702821186564" style="display:none">First book in the series, and I really liked it!<br /><br />When I found out that DeMille wrote The General's Daughter, I did a little more research on his 'John Corey' series. It seems that he hadn't wanted to write a series, but there were too many of his readers who wanted another John Corey book. He'd been afraid of his female readers; what they'd think of John as a character. He's cocky, tactless, crude, and a real ass, but I adored him. I loved how his mind worked, how he processed what he saw, what he heard, what he read. As much of a jerk he can be, it made him who he is, and I don't think I could have asked for a better character.<br /><br />I thought Beth as a good equal for him. She gave back as good as she got, and I think John needed that.<br /><br />I was glad that John met Emma. He needed her in more ways that the obvious. I think it made him a better person.<br /><br />There was a twist in this plot, one that I didn't see coming, and at first, I had the 'yeah, right' thought about it. But the more the direction of the story went that way, the more I believed and the more I liked the plot.<br /><br />Wasn't all that surprised by who the killer was, but I liked how John dealt with him and the situation. The action was great. I'm definitely getting the rest of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10609822702821186564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_579660605" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/579660605" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/951102-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1204385107p2/951102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/579660605?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/951102-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/951102-stephen?shelf=pop-lit">pop-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/951102-stephen?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/951102-stephen?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/951102-stephen?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer579660605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9919946766530078725">With this novel I've got beef. Let's begin!<br/><br/>1. It's twice as long as it needs to be. 700+ pages is an absurd length for a standard suspense/detective novel. And there's nothing special about this novel from a narrative standpoint to warrant this kind of length. There's an initial mystery; some intriguing facts; the plot thickens; TWIST!; plot comes together; bad guy revealed; final encounter; resolution. I've read dozens upon dozens of books with this format, and I would be hard pressed to find a</span>
  <span id="freeText9919946766530078725" style="display:none">With this novel I've got beef. Let's begin!<br /><br />1. It's twice as long as it needs to be. 700+ pages is an absurd length for a standard suspense/detective novel. And there's nothing special about this novel from a narrative standpoint to warrant this kind of length. There's an initial mystery; some intriguing facts; the plot thickens; TWIST!; plot comes together; bad guy revealed; final encounter; resolution. I've read dozens upon dozens of books with this format, and I would be hard pressed to find any that cracked 400 pages.<br /><br />2. <i>So it's really long. What does DeMille do with all of that extra space?</i> Well, faithful reader, I'm glad you asked. The answer is, he listens to himself talk. There is so much time spent on just how "witty" and "likeable" and street smart John Corey (our hero) is that you can't help but get the sense that DeMille wishes he were him. <br /><br />I put "witty" and "likeable" in quotes because, after 300 pages of being inside John's head, he is anything but these things. First off, here's a guy who never met a bad or sexist or dirty or obvious joke he didn't like, and he dropped them every single chance he got. <br /><br />What else about John Corey? Here is a list of adjectives you could apply to him easily (some of which he applied to himself directly): sexist, chauvinist, elitist, crude, rude, arrogant, offensive, antagonistic, alcoholic, cocksure, egotistic, and obnoxious.<br /><br />The problem with this is that DeMille presents most of these attributes as endearing, suggesting that Corey's just a regular guy you'd like to have a beer with. The problem is, he's an ass. He's a jerk to everyone. He gives attitude in every single interaction he has in the book, but he hates it when someone gives it back. He looks down his nose at the well off because they like wine and fine food when he just wants a beer and a burger. He's irresistible to no less than two women, and even though he's his usual self around them, they just can't help but love him. He hates old people. He hates smart people. He hates rich people. He hates other security people. And those he does like, you don't really know why.<br /><br />Also, he's the greatest thing that's ever happened to police work. He knows all the right lines to work. He finds all the leads. He asks all the right questions and makes all the right assumptions. Now, granted, this is nothing new in stories like this. It's not much fun when your hero detective is clueless. But good novels allow a give and take. The hero gets the majority of the clues, but his colleagues and partners make significant contributions. In this novel? Corey's main partner is simply there. Any contributions she makes are ancillary and really don't add anything. Its the Superman problem. A flawless hero is boring.<br /><br />3. The plot doesn't make much sense. If you just let the story wash over your without asking any questions, then sure, you won't notice anything. If you pause even briefly to poke at the mystery plot on which the novel is built, it's not long before water starts gushing through.<br /><br />4. I could go on, but I won't...<br /><br />5. Well, actually, one last thing, because it's a big one.<br /><br /><b>***HERE THERE BE SPOILERS***</b><br /><br />At the end of the novel, Corey chases down the bad guy, intent on killing him. The bad guy's killed a lot of people and raped and killed Corey's girlfriend of 3 days. (The whole rape thing, while awful, seems out of place when it's presented. It's like DeMille wanted to really drive home how evil the bad guy is and need to tack something else horrific to his rap sheet because killing no less than 6 people wasn't enough.) Corey wants his revenge, and after outwitting the bad guy in an impossible situation, Corey takes a knife, breaks the bad guy's nose and mouth, scalps him (Corey didn't like that he had hair plugs.), and then guts him. Yes, that's right, he guts him. He takes the knife and slices open his abdomen; then grabs the bad guy's intestines, pulls them out, and throws them in the bad guy's face. Then he walks away leaving him to die.<br /><br />First off, this is pretty brutal. Second, if the bad guy dies, it's 1st degree murder. <br /><br />Anyway, the cops arrive, Corey tells them where the bad guy is and that he left him for dead. Surprise! The bad guy's still alive and is arrested and sent to prison to await trial. And now you'd expect Corey to be put in prison as well, right? Right? Wait, what? He gets pats on the back and is rewarded as a hero cop?!? <br /><br />In what world would this fly? Corey didn't just try to kill him. He tortured and mutilated him. It's not as though he shot him with his service pistol in the line of duty. He sadistically tortured him with the intent to leave him dead. But the novel presents this as an OK thing! It's a mind-boggling ending!<br /><br />Anyway, that's where the book ends. The world goes back to normal, and there are apparently more John Corey novels to come, because he's so great. I should point out that <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/93788.Night_Fall__John_Corey___3_" title="Night Fall (John Corey, #3) by Nelson DeMille" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Fall</a> is one of those books, and THAT was maybe one of the most offensive books I've ever read in my life. (Also, surprisingly, a book that suffers from the same issues as this one. You'd think I'd learn my lesson.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9919946766530078725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1191427524" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1191427524" />
    <a title="Freda Malone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6938113-freda-malone"><img alt="Freda Malone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418039583p2/6938113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1191427524?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Freda Malone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Freda Malone" href="/user/show/6938113-freda-malone">Freda Malone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780446605403" href="/book/show/685453.Plum_Island">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6938113-freda-malone?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1191427524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7880728899271487036">John Corey is convalescing at his Uncle Harry's Victorian home in the North Fork of Long Island, NY. The Suffolk County Chief, Sylvester Maxwell (Max) has asked John to be a consultant in a double homicide. John learns it is friends of his, Tom and Judy Gordon. A delightful couple who worked at the infamous Plum Island Research Facility for the Department of Agriculture studying animal diseases, viruses and flu's. Immediately, there are several people involved, Foster (FBI), Nash (DOA), Detectiv</span>
  <span id="freeText7880728899271487036" style="display:none">John Corey is convalescing at his Uncle Harry's Victorian home in the North Fork of Long Island, NY. The Suffolk County Chief, Sylvester Maxwell (Max) has asked John to be a consultant in a double homicide. John learns it is friends of his, Tom and Judy Gordon. A delightful couple who worked at the infamous Plum Island Research Facility for the Department of Agriculture studying animal diseases, viruses and flu's. Immediately, there are several people involved, Foster (FBI), Nash (DOA), Detective Penrose, Detective Maxwell, and then there is John and it seems as though there are too many people in the 'kitchen', stepping on each others toes. Each character has their own theory, biological weapon of smuggled out Ebola virus, drugs and drug runners along the bay, archaeological weapons from the revolutionary war. <br /><br />I really enjoyed the wide array of characters and their personalities. John Corey is an obnoxious, witty, sarcastic man who shoots his mouth off at the most inopportune times, but it made me laugh. I really liked his sense of humor throughout the whole book. His instinct is right on the money and he keeps these clues and conclusions to himself, most of the time. I also liked Emma, the the town's president of the Historical Society who had a lot of knowledge about 'old' Plum Island, Captain Kidd, Battles won and lost, Treasure maps and who settled where first. I absorbed it like a sponge hoping her knowledge would give me more clues to the possible suspects. Nash, who claims he is from the Department of Agriculture, is not who he seems and he is a cocky and arrogant who dislikes John at first sight. Beth Penrose was very smart, likable but serious about her job. <br /><br />While everyone else is running around gathering evidence from town folk, John is doing his own thing and eventually solves the puzzle and I'm thinking, "Damn, why didn't I think of that?!". A couple of things I did not see coming, which made it that much more puzzling but enjoyable. It was a little sad, scary, had some suspense toward the end but had it not been for the humor of John, it would have been a tiring story with a lot of background and very long. It kept me entertained and I couldn't wait to find out what John figured out toward the end. I do believe this will be another one on my favorites list and will soon be picking up the next in the series. <br /><br />I'd recommend this book to anyone who likes historical mystery thrillers, with a bit of humor and biological science mixed in. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7880728899271487036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_89544558" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89544558" />
    <a title="Brandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3050414-brandi"><img alt="Brandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1264203450p2/3050414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89544558?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandi" href="/user/show/3050414-brandi">Brandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89544558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12883178498671645083">I was hoping that both of the main characters (especially the narrator) would drown so the book would end sooner.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_937279038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/937279038" />
    <a title="Tim The Enchanter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5654692-tim-the-enchanter"><img alt="Tim The Enchanter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386188040p2/5654692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/937279038?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim The Enchanter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim The Enchanter" href="/user/show/5654692-tim-the-enchanter">Tim The Enchanter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="MP3 Book 9781607889731" href="/book/show/9851276-plum-island-unabridged">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer937279038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8539536618652145801"><b>
  <u> Something, Whatever, You Know - 4 Stars </u>
</b><br/><br/>Despite a vocabulary that included more non-specific words than a valley girl, I found myself amused and entertained by John Corey. Both irreverent and brilliant, Corey is one of the most entertaining protagonists I have read in a long time. Because of my preference for reading lesser know authors, I have put off reading this series for a long time. Fortunately, it was well written and entertaining and I will certainly continue the series.<br/><br/><b> Plot Summar</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8539536618652145801" style="display:none"><b>
  <u> Something, Whatever, You Know - 4 Stars </u>
</b><br /><br />Despite a vocabulary that included more non-specific words than a valley girl, I found myself amused and entertained by John Corey. Both irreverent and brilliant, Corey is one of the most entertaining protagonists I have read in a long time. Because of my preference for reading lesser know authors, I have put off reading this series for a long time. Fortunately, it was well written and entertaining and I will certainly continue the series.<br /><br /><b> Plot Summary </b><br /><br />John Corey is a New York Homicide Detective. After being shot in the line of duty, he head offs to his uncles house on Long Island while he convalesces. Rest does not come easy after a two recently made friends are murdered in what is initially called a bungled home invasion. Had this husband and wife duo been simple fishermen, the investigation would have ended there. In this case, the deceased are two brilliant scientists working on Plum Island. Plum Island is rumored to be working on everything from biological warfare research, vaccine research to planning the next plague. It becomes clear that the murders are tied in some way to plum island and John is brought in by the local sheriff to advise on the case. Never believing the official line, John Corey works with local detective Beth Penrose to follow his own line of reasoning while at the same time dodging the federal agents working the case. John battles man and nature as the case takes him down an unlikely path.<br /><br /><b> My Take </b><br /><br />Overall, this is an exceptionally written and entertaining novel. John Corey is a funny and intelligent while occasionally being a jackass. Prior to this novel, I did not know that a place called Plum Island existed. It is in realty an island run by the USDA where they undertake research into animal disease. Take any government research facility and place it on a small island and people will spin rumors all day. I thought the setting of Long Island and Plum Island were excellent choice and vibrantly written.<br /><br />Nelson DeMille is quite masterful in his use of dialogue. It is written in a manner that is captivating and is perfectly suited for audio (which is the format I used.) The character interactions are realistic and the exchanges are usually funny. John has a habit of using non specific narration. For example, "I looked to my left on the boat, or the starboard, or the stern or whatever the heck it's called". While entertaining in the first half, it does start to become annoying later in the book and is (in my opinion) overused.<br /><br />I found the plot and the setup to be well crafted and realistic. My only issue was I didn't buy John's "Eureka" moment when he seemed to discovered what was really going on. I just don't know how the heck he figured out what was really happening. It seems as if he was relying on some sixth sense. Given the content, the plot could have easily degenerated into a hokey mess but the author did a great job of using plot elements that could have taken the story down.<br /><br /><b> Final Thoughts </b><br /><br />Overall, <i> Plum Island </i> in an entertaining and very well written novel. There is nothing to complex or obscure in the novel and should appeal to a wide range of readers. I am a bit late in getting to the series but I will certainly be reading more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8539536618652145801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9663059309129117121">My first book my author Nelson De Mille, and also my first with the great witty character John Corley, and a great end to the 2014 book pal reads for me, so thank you Book Pal friends.<br/><br/>Wounded in the line of duty, NYPD homicide cop John Corey is convalescing in rural eastern Long Island when an attractive young couple he knows is found shot to death on the family patio. The victims were biologists at Plum Island, a research site rumoured to be an incubator for germ warfare. Suddenly, a local doub</span>
  <span id="freeText9663059309129117121" style="display:none">My first book my author Nelson De Mille, and also my first with the great witty character John Corley, and a great end to the 2014 book pal reads for me, so thank you Book Pal friends.<br /><br />Wounded in the line of duty, NYPD homicide cop John Corey is convalescing in rural eastern Long Island when an attractive young couple he knows is found shot to death on the family patio. The victims were biologists at Plum Island, a research site rumoured to be an incubator for germ warfare. Suddenly, a local double murder takes on shattering global implications — and thrusts Corey and two extraordinary women into a dangerous search for the secret of PLUM ISLAND....<br /><br />But beyond all of that lies at its heart one of the most engaging hero's ever conceived: John Corey. His manners are scratched and his jokes are annoying to everyone (except to himself and the reader), but still comes off as an intelligent and competent vacationing cop who gets embroiled in the mystery involving a couple who worked on Plum Island- an animal disease compound that hides more than Ebola and Anthrax. <br /><br />Well written, great detail, a great main character in John Corley, just to me fifty to hundred pages to long mainly in the middle of the story, but a great rip roaring storm filled ending.<br /><br />Must read the other John Corley books.</span>

<div id="review_789252892" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/789252892" />
    <a title="Luffy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy"><img alt="Luffy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606210775p2/7407364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/789252892?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luffy" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy">Luffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=page-turner">page-turner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=chunkster">chunkster</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=pretty-good">pretty-good</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer789252892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12278451109211945929"> Plum island, truth be told, exceeded my expectations. Except in the humor department. The latter isn't the one thing I look forward to in a thriller anyway. Any book can be written in any style. There's one style, a bleak, grim and unapologetic style that I flee from like a vampire from the sun. Books that imitate life. It can crop up in any book. Fortunately, Plum Island is not like that; it is simply peachy. Oh, and if you want to read this book, you can omit Chapter 13. There's quite some de</span>
  <span id="freeText12278451109211945929" style="display:none"> Plum island, truth be told, exceeded my expectations. Except in the humor department. The latter isn't the one thing I look forward to in a thriller anyway. Any book can be written in any style. There's one style, a bleak, grim and unapologetic style that I flee from like a vampire from the sun. Books that imitate life. It can crop up in any book. Fortunately, Plum Island is not like that; it is simply peachy. Oh, and if you want to read this book, you can omit Chapter 13. There's quite some delay tactic going on in Chapter 13, but after that it's all plain sailing. <br /><br /> In the past I would take issue with a hero like John Corey. He seems too loyal and kind, while being too egocentric, too flawed. I didn't really understand this type of person before. But now I've experienced it first hand; people that are incredibly generous and kind of kind, while being of ordinary mettle at their core. Nevertheless, I was dreading being cooped up in John Corey's mind for 500 pages. But the sharp cynicism and witticisms got relegated to the back of the decor and the intrigue took center stage. Although I AM wondering if I should give this book a perfect score. But though it was a good book, it didn't have the unexpected, the original, the ultra ribald, or the hair raise inducing bits. You know I still think that John Corey is not real. Like the saying goes, read it once, fooled me once, read it twice, will fool me twice. So there will be no re read. Ta.</span>

I love his writing style and how he involves some comedy in his books, I even laughed out loud at some of the funny parts.<br/><br/>John Corey to me was like a Bruce Willis type guy, I was really impressed with his character. I look forward to reading more by Nelson Demille!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/947897023?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo" href="/user/show/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo">Anne  (Booklady) Molinarolo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780446605403" href="/book/show/685453.Plum_Island">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=permanent-library">permanent-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=anne-booklady-500-page-books">anne-booklady-500-page-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=spring-2015">spring-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=good-fiction">good-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3615945-anne-booklady-molinarolo?shelf=thriller-mystery">thriller-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer947897023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5237599437512657433"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br/> <br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille' title='Nelson DeMille' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nelson DeMille</a> has created a wonderful character - John Corey! <i>"I think I'm in love."</i> Corey isn't your usual loner, introverted, and serious dark homicide detective. He's snarky. He's smart mouthed. He's juvenile. He appears to be a bumbling idiot just like Peter Falk's character - Columbo. He's smart and is narcissistic, but I loved him! Being in his head for over 600 pages was fun and I've never laughed so hard during a novel in a long time, even though the plot line was serious, dea</span>
  <span id="freeText5237599437512657433" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br /> <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille" title="Nelson DeMille" rel="nofollow noopener">Nelson DeMille</a> has created a wonderful character - John Corey! <i>"I think I'm in love."</i> Corey isn't your usual loner, introverted, and serious dark homicide detective. He's snarky. He's smart mouthed. He's juvenile. He appears to be a bumbling idiot just like Peter Falk's character - Columbo. He's smart and is narcissistic, but I loved him! Being in his head for over 600 pages was fun and I've never laughed so hard during a novel in a long time, even though the plot line was serious, deadly serious.<br /> <br />Tom and Judy Gorgon are good friends of convalescing NYPD Detective John Corey. They are beautiful. They are brilliant. They work on Plum Island. Apparently, they are also thieves, since they're also very dead. Both shot in the head on their deck as they were climbing from their Formula 300 at the dock. Their big silver cooler is missing from their boat. A Jolly Roger flag and signal pennants are flying. Could they have stolen an animal virus from Plum Island that bad guys could weaponize? Suits from the Alphabet Departments have decided the cover story - the Doctors Gordon stole a vaccine that rightly belongs to the U.S. Government to sell or go with them to a private sector pharmaceutical company. John Corey doesn't believe either of these theories and is determined to find out what happened to his friends. Thank goodness he's been asked to consult on the case. Then he's fired. But why? And by whom? At whose suggestion? Does Corey drop the case? Of course not.<br /> <br />I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille" title="Nelson DeMille" rel="nofollow noopener">Nelson DeMille</a> slow build up of the mystery. He gives you a few red herrings and several twists and turns. He does a great job of building characters, both the minor and major ones. He uses the first person POV and it was a treat and hoot to be in John Corey's head. I definitely <u>must</u> read the rest of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/52228-john-corey" rel="nofollow noopener">John Corey Series</a>! And I recommend readers who love Thrillers do the same. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5237599437512657433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17671190614108113441">In July of 2017, I chanced upon John Corey, the character in DeMille’s main series, in the collection of short mysteries of that year entitled "Matchup." His basic humanity, in part veiled by and in part revealed by his wisecracking attitude, his anti-PC stance, and lightning quick mind struck chords with me.   <span id="freeText17671190614108113441" style="display:none">In July of 2017, I chanced upon John Corey, the character in DeMille’s main series, in the collection of short mysteries of that year entitled "Matchup." His basic humanity, in part veiled by and in part revealed by his wisecracking attitude, his anti-PC stance, and lightning quick mind struck chords with me. So, I read the first book of the series, Plum Island. That sold me and I then read straight through all of the books in the series.<br /><br />Plum Island (Corey Book 1) is a touch predictable in the sense that it plays off of the germ warfare facility on that island, but it nevertheless achieves a fresh arc – involving buried treasure, no less – and puts former NYPD detective John Corey on full display. If you like fun poked at political correctness you will love Corey.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1534075177?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/545336-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=xcharity-2016">xcharity-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=great-thriller-reads">great-thriller-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1534075177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16241290375031117459">Crap! <b>4 Stars</b> for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33810.Plum_Island__John_Corey___1_' title='Plum Island (John Corey, #1) by Nelson DeMille' rel='nofollow noopener'>Plum Island</a>. Now I have to add DeMille to that list, you know, the list with Child, Connolly, Connelly, Sandford, Hiaasen, Mills, Block, et al. The list of prolific authors who I have to buy on sight. At least I can fix the blame for this one on Anne Booklady and on Steven Z who both recommended it. Thanks a lot, no really, thanks!<br/><br/>John Corey is a smart ass cop, recovering from multiple holes in his body caused by small pieces of high speed lead. You will keep hearing little tid</span>
  <span id="freeText16241290375031117459" style="display:none">Crap! <b>4 Stars</b> for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33810.Plum_Island__John_Corey___1_" title="Plum Island (John Corey, #1) by Nelson DeMille" rel="nofollow noopener">Plum Island</a>. Now I have to add DeMille to that list, you know, the list with Child, Connolly, Connelly, Sandford, Hiaasen, Mills, Block, et al. The list of prolific authors who I have to buy on sight. At least I can fix the blame for this one on Anne Booklady and on Steven Z who both recommended it. Thanks a lot, no really, thanks!<br /><br />John Corey is a smart ass cop, recovering from multiple holes in his body caused by small pieces of high speed lead. You will keep hearing little tidbits about the event that caused his physical status but never the full story. Maybe in a later book? Meanwhile, Corey is hired at a $1 a month to assist on a double homicide of scientists (a married couple) who worked at the Plum Island (real nasty, secret, ominous, "we don't do biological warfare") Animal Research Center. I laughed hard at many points in the story. Corey is constantly wisecracking, driving his various partners to distraction. <br /><br />The other characters in the book are well done. I especially fell in love (or more likely another "L" word) with Emma, a winsome local on the North Fork of Long Island. Corey also falls for Emma, as he talks about going back to her cottage for the evening:<br /><br /><i>Anyway, the cottage was cute, it was clean, there was no cat, she had scotch and beer, the mattress was firm, she liked the Beatles and the Bee Gees; and she had two pillows for me. What more could I ask? Well, whipped cream. She had that, too.</i><br /><br />I only took most of a star away for the end of the book, Corey gets way out of control for a cop and the frenetic chase scene really didn't need to go so over the top. But I will be buying more of DeMille's John Corey series, darn it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16241290375031117459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
