<div id="review_13867213" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/13867213" />
    <a title="Leslie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/846253-leslie"><img alt="Leslie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504671639p2/846253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/13867213?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leslie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leslie" href="/user/show/846253-leslie">Leslie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/4982066-plum-island">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer13867213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15779793614376922642">This is the FIRST John Corey book. so it is a MUST READ. Here we are introduced to Mr. Corey who is recovering from a near death experience at the hands of some gang members on the streets of NY at his uncle's north shore farm. He's been relaxing, tanning and making new friends. Two of his new friends are scientists at Plum Island. Plum Island is (was) part of the USDA animal quarantine and testing labs. Plum Island sits off shore at a former fort and depending on your conspiracy level is a wond</span>
  <span id="freeText15779793614376922642" style="display:none">This is the FIRST John Corey book. so it is a MUST READ. Here we are introduced to Mr. Corey who is recovering from a near death experience at the hands of some gang members on the streets of NY at his uncle's north shore farm. He's been relaxing, tanning and making new friends. Two of his new friends are scientists at Plum Island. Plum Island is (was) part of the USDA animal quarantine and testing labs. Plum Island sits off shore at a former fort and depending on your conspiracy level is a wonderful place that keeps us safe or a dangerous place full of crazy people who are genetically modifying diseases that will kill us deader than dead. <br /><br />When these two scientists end up dead and definitely murdered the local police ask Corey to take a look. So he gets roped into an investigation that will have him facing death and discovering that there is a lot of evil in the bucolic beach towns </span>
  <a data-text-id="15779793614376922642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15230305109132552262" style="display:none">I can't believe it - Spenser has moved to NYC and joined the police force. He tried to fool me by changing his name to John Corey, and even the author's name from Robert B. Parker, but I recognize his wisecracking ways anywhere.<br /><br />OK, well false alarm, but John Corey certainly reminded me of Spenser in a lot of ways. Even as he's about to die, he can't help making jokes and insulting his assailants, but he's often pretty funny and perhaps a little more modern in his lack of PC. Overall, I enjoyed the humor, and some of it was not even too corny. But if I were to try to take the stories too seriously, I'd probably think it's a bit over the top, so my advice is not take this (or anything) too seriously.<br /><br />But all kidding aside, it was an interesting story that held my attention and I learned a few things along the way. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer197572582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4734519220625998025">Ah...sarcastic narrators. This book's got one. <br/><br/><blockquote>"I gripped my right ear and twisted, which is how I tune out idiots."</blockquote><br/><br/>Unfortunately, it's apparent that everyone <i>except</i> John Corey (our fearless, convalescing-from-getting-shot-on-the-job narrator/hero) is an idiot. I sorta wish that his ear had been turned off for some larger chunks of the book -- because the reader has to wade through a lot of red herrings and <i>schtuff</i> to get to the meat of the book.<br/><br/>For example, getting a tour of Plum Island, the sp</span>
  <span id="freeText4734519220625998025" style="display:none">Ah...sarcastic narrators. This book's got one. <br /><br /><blockquote>"I gripped my right ear and twisted, which is how I tune out idiots."</blockquote><br /><br />Unfortunately, it's apparent that everyone <i>except</i> John Corey (our fearless, convalescing-from-getting-shot-on-the-job narrator/hero) is an idiot. I sorta wish that his ear had been turned off for some larger chunks of the book -- because the reader has to wade through a lot of red herrings and <i>schtuff</i> to get to the meat of the book.<br /><br />For example, getting a tour of Plum Island, the spot where world-threatening viruses are studied and possibly stolen, shouldn't be so long and tedious. For an example of that: there are numerous mentions of the ospreys -- but don't get all excited. It's not a clue. Apparently the bird has nothing more to do with the story than a narrative motif, which doesn't quite come off for me. The tour of Plum Island takes 100 pages and by the time you reach the end, witty repartee like<br /><br /><blockquote>"I had to ask, 'But is the female screwworm fulfilled?'<br />'She must be,' Zollner replied. 'She never mates again.'<br />Beth offered, 'There's another way to look at that.'"</blockquote><br /><br />is just a little frustrating. You want INFORMATION, not wit, by that point.<br /><br />That being said, the characters are certainly likeable (you know, except for the ones you're not supposed to like) <br /><br />And even the false leads are intriguing. Pirate treasure, virus hunting, international intrigue, historical implications, etc. You just can't get much better than that. The whole thing is an adventurer's wet dream. It's fun to go and figure stuff out along with Corey -- though the turn might be a little to easy to catch. I mean, I got the gist before they left Plum Island...which might explain why a lot of the copious detail felt, well, <i>copious</i>. <br /><br />~Jenny<br /><a href="http://www.placeforthestolen.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Place for the Stolen</a><br /><a href="http://www.undergroundwritingproject.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Under Ground Writing Project</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4734519220625998025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer181353170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18299527308754938879">This is a book I just didn't want to like. There were corny lines throughout this 570+ page monster of a book, maybe excusable because it was first person narrative and not the author. I'm much more a minimalist than this kind of lengthy work and yet the writing was too simple with parts I felt were rushed and even lazy. This is the kind of writing you learn not to write in MFA programs, yet it sells, and it sells well, and for good reasons. I found myself wanting to know the outcome of the char</span>
  <span id="freeText18299527308754938879" style="display:none">This is a book I just didn't want to like. There were corny lines throughout this 570+ page monster of a book, maybe excusable because it was first person narrative and not the author. I'm much more a minimalist than this kind of lengthy work and yet the writing was too simple with parts I felt were rushed and even lazy. This is the kind of writing you learn not to write in MFA programs, yet it sells, and it sells well, and for good reasons. I found myself wanting to know the outcome of the characters, even the unlikable narrator John Corey. DeMille hooked me in the first chapter. That's all it took. There was nothing I could do to get out. Despite saying I was going to drop the book after another chapter or two, I kept going right to the end. The setting describes the small town feel of eastern Long Island, which was a lure to the book in the first place (since I grew up on LI). You also see these big selling authors who you've never read, or even heard uttered in the MFA academic world, and you get curious. -half a star for the addictive quality -half a star for the unlikable narrator and dialogue</span>
  <a data-text-id="18299527308754938879" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UN58qaKnncs3dMyuuLzczwNofwL3v/Pit9TakX8hJ/P8zrVEH5bFgzZBQ6k69LrSKqD1ScI1/kt53+T0xIhdDA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

To have no memory of ever being alone.”\n\nTwin sisters Bibike and Ariyike are enjoying a relatively comfortable life in Lagos in 1996. Then their mother loses her job due to political strife, and the family, facing poverty, becomes drawn into the New Church, an institution led by a charismatic pastor who is not shy about worshipping earthly wealth. \n\nSoon Bibike and Ariyike’s father wagers the family home on a “sure bet” that evaporates like smoke. As their parents’ marriage collapses in the aftermath of this gamble, the twin sisters and their two younger siblings, Andrew and Peter, are thrust into the reluctant care of their traditional Yoruba grandmother. Inseparable while they had their parents to care for them, the twins’ paths diverge once the household shatters. Each girl is left to locate, guard, and hone her own fragile source of power. \n\nWritten with astonishing intimacy and wry attention to the fickleness of fate, Tola Rotimi Abraham’s Black Sunday takes us into the chaotic heart of family life, tracing a line from the euphoria of kinship to the devastation of estrangement. In the process, it joyfully tells a tale of grace and connection in the midst of daily oppression and the constant incursions of an unremitting patriarchy. This is a novel about two young women slowly finding, over twenty years, in a place rife with hypocrisy but also endless life and love, their own distinct methods of resistance and paths to       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille">About Nelson DeMille</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1498066748p3/1238.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2563342979890736173">Nelson Richard DeMille was born in New York City on August 23, 1943 to Huron and Antonia (Panzera) DeMille, then moved with his parents to Long Island. He graduated from Elmont Memorial High School, where he played football and ran track.<br/><br/>DeMille spent three years at Hofstra University, then joined the Army where he attended Officer Candidate School and was commissioned a Lieutenant in the United S</span>
  <span id="freeText2563342979890736173" style="display:none">Nelson Richard DeMille was born in New York City on August 23, 1943 to Huron and Antonia (Panzera) DeMille, then moved with his parents to Long Island. He graduated from Elmont Memorial High School, where he played football and ran track.<br /><br />DeMille spent three years at Hofstra University, then joined the Army where he attended Officer Candidate School and was commissioned a Lieutenant in the United States Army (1966-69). He saw action in Vietnam as an infantry platoon leader with the First Cavalry Division and was decorated with the Air Medal, Bronze Star, and the Vietnamese Cross of Gallantry.<br /><br />After his discharge, DeMille returned to Hofstra University where he received his bachelor’s degree in Political Science and History. He has three children, Lauren, Alexander, and James, and resides on Long Island.<br /><br />DeMille's first major novel was By the Rivers of Babylon, published in 1978, and is still in print as are all his succeeding novels. He is a member of American Mensa, The Authors Guild, and is past president of the Mystery Writers of America. He is also a member of International Thriller Writers and was chosen as ThrillerMaster of the Year 2015. He holds three honorary doctorates: Doctor of Humane Letters from Hofstra University, Doctor of Literature from Long Island University, and Doctor of Humane Letters from Dowling College.<br /><br />Nelson DeMille is the author of: By the Rivers of Babylon, Cathedral, The Talbot Odyssey, Word of Honor, The Charm School, The Gold Coast, The General's Daughter, Spencerville, Plum Island, The Lion's Game, Up Country, Night Fall, Wild Fire, The Gate House, The Lion, The Panther, The Quest, Radiant Angel, The Cuban Affair and The Deserter. He also co-authored Mayday with Thomas Block and has contributed short stories to anthologies, and book reviews and articles to magazines and newspapers.</span>
